<div id="review_993376237" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/993376237" />
    <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira"><img alt="Ivonne Rovira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339470651p2/3803671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/993376237?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivonne Rovira" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira">Ivonne Rovira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6620556-when-you-reach-me">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ivonne by: </span>
      Lisa Eggers
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3803671-ivonne-rovira?shelf=children-literature">children-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer993376237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3299182848949588519">In a conventional novel for young people, Miranda Sinclair’s mother practicing to be a contestant on <i>The $20,000 Pyramid</i> would be the highlight — nay, the entirety — of the novel. But by now you’ve guessed that <i>When You Reach Me</i> is no ordinary novel; instead, it’s one of the most unconventional novels I’ve ever read — and I’m including <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/119073.The_Name_of_the_Rose' title='The Name of the Rose by Umberto Eco' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Name of the Rose</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/192528.The_Icarus_Hunt' title='The Icarus Hunt by Timothy Zahn' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Icarus Hunt</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/378498.Dorp_Dead' title='Dorp Dead by Julia Cunningham' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dorp Dead</a>, and Miranda’s favorite book of all time, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18131.A_Wrinkle_in_Time__A_Wrinkle_in_Time_Quintet___1_' title='A Wrinkle in Time (A Wrinkle in Time Quintet, #1) by Madeleine L'Engle' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Wrinkle in Time</a>. Miranda’s mother, a bleeding-heart paralegal and sin</span>
  <span id="freeText3299182848949588519" style="display:none">In a conventional novel for young people, Miranda Sinclair’s mother practicing to be a contestant on <i>The $20,000 Pyramid</i> would be the highlight — nay, the entirety — of the novel. But by now you’ve guessed that <i>When You Reach Me</i> is no ordinary novel; instead, it’s one of the most unconventional novels I’ve ever read — and I’m including <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/119073.The_Name_of_the_Rose" title="The Name of the Rose by Umberto Eco" rel="nofollow noopener">The Name of the Rose</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/192528.The_Icarus_Hunt" title="The Icarus Hunt by Timothy Zahn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Icarus Hunt</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/378498.Dorp_Dead" title="Dorp Dead by Julia Cunningham" rel="nofollow noopener">Dorp Dead</a>, and Miranda’s favorite book of all time, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18131.A_Wrinkle_in_Time__A_Wrinkle_in_Time_Quintet___1_" title="A Wrinkle in Time (A Wrinkle in Time Quintet, #1) by Madeleine L'Engle" rel="nofollow noopener">A Wrinkle in Time</a>. Miranda’s mother, a bleeding-heart paralegal and single mom, <i>does</i> achieve her dream of garnering a spot on the ABC game show, but that fact is dwarfed by the main point of the novel, which doesn’t reveal itself until two-thirds of the way through. <br /><br /><i>When You Reach Me</i> is best enjoyed when the reader goes in without knowing much. But I can reveal that the novel dwells on how a small act can profoundly affect those around you, for good or ill. That what has become a platitude can be expressed so profoundly and uniquely is a testament to author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/175329.Rebecca_Stead" title="Rebecca Stead" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebecca Stead</a>’s talent. Miranda and her friends Sal, Annemarie, Colin, Marcus Heilbronner, and Julia — whether in their pettiness or superciliousness or self-absorbed cruelty or bad-boy misunderstood pose — will strike the reader as real kids, with all the rough edges and inexplicable kindnesses and cruelties that that implies. Whether you’re an adult or child, this will be one of the more original works you’ll ever read.<br /><br />So why four stars and not five? The book didn’t reach me emotionally in the same way as, say, <i>The Wrinkle in Time</i> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4581447.The_Ring_of_Rocamadour__The_Red_Blazer_Girls___1_" title="The Ring of Rocamadour (The Red Blazer Girls, #1) by Michael D. Beil" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ring of Rocamadour</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1809175.The_Magic_Thief__Magic_Thief___1_" title="The Magic Thief (Magic Thief, #1) by Sarah Prineas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Magic Thief</a> did, although I can’t quite put my finger on why. As a native New Yorker, I should have fallen in love with this chronicle of New York City’s West Side in 1978, but I never did. Perhaps, like Charles Wallace Murray in <i>The Wrinkle in Time</i>, I somehow just couldn’t connect. But I suspect that the mystery didn’t start building too late for me to become swept up in the book. Still, very much recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3299182848949588519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Shannon by: </span>
      Andy
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=good-but-will-never-reread">good-but-will-never-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=award-winner">award-winner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=color-red">color-red</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67569437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14610194477663836533"><b>4.5 stars!</b><br/><br/>This is the newest Newbery Medal Award Winner and I had actually wanted to read it before it had been nominated. <b>This is a cleverly written "slice of life" tale that transcends age, gender, and race and is a great story that anyone and everyone can enjoy.</b><br/><br/>This book twists and turns and meanders about in such a fascinating way that you're quickly pulled into Miranda's and her friends' lives and what it's like to grow up in New York in the late '70s. Some of the observations that the auth</span>
  <span id="freeText14610194477663836533" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars!</b><br /><br />This is the newest Newbery Medal Award Winner and I had actually wanted to read it before it had been nominated. <b>This is a cleverly written "slice of life" tale that transcends age, gender, and race and is a great story that anyone and everyone can enjoy.</b><br /><br />This book twists and turns and meanders about in such a fascinating way that you're quickly pulled into Miranda's and her friends' lives and what it's like to grow up in New York in the late '70s. Some of the observations that the author made were so random yet nostalgic for me that I felt transported back to elementary school. I connected with the characters in a way that doesn't happen all that often with children's books for me anymore, and I'm not sure if that's because I'm getting older or if I'm just not reading that many great children's books anymore. This sort of reminded me of how I felt when I read Roald Dahl; he didn't dumb things down for kids and he knew how to write a great story.<br /><br />T<b>he only reason I didn't give this 5 stars was because of the main conclusion at the end.</b> I think I wanted something a little more realistic and I was hoping the author was going to tie things up in a different way than I saw playing out. Don't get me wrong though, the end didn't spoil the book for me, I just felt like things could have gone differently.<br /><br />I think a lot of people will enjoy this book for years to come; it's funny, heart-warming, at times sad, and has a great mystery as well. This is one book that I can say is totally deserving of its award! </span>
  <a data-text-id="14610194477663836533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" href="/user/show/289556-jackie-the-librarian">Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289556-jackie-the-librarian?shelf=sciencefiction">sciencefiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289556-jackie-the-librarian?shelf=childrensbooks">childrensbooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289556-jackie-the-librarian?shelf=awardwinners">awardwinners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289556-jackie-the-librarian?shelf=timetravel">timetravel</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99503516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer228928177361781084">I just finished this, and I'm feeling like I missed something. So many people are raving about this, but I don't see it. I liked the New York setting, the kids running around on their own with latch keys, and the visits to the sub shop at lunch time. The friendships and characters were good, but didn't seem remarkable. <br/>The story is about Miranda, who lives with her mom in New York, and whose favorite book is <i>A Wrinkle in Time</i>, which is one of my favorite books, too. Her mom wants to get on the $</span>
  <span id="freeText228928177361781084" style="display:none">I just finished this, and I'm feeling like I missed something. So many people are raving about this, but I don't see it. I liked the New York setting, the kids running around on their own with latch keys, and the visits to the sub shop at lunch time. The friendships and characters were good, but didn't seem remarkable. <br />The story is about Miranda, who lives with her mom in New York, and whose favorite book is <i>A Wrinkle in Time</i>, which is one of my favorite books, too. Her mom wants to get on the $50,000 Pyramid game show, and manages to get picked as a contestant. Miranda and her mom's boyfriend help her practice.<br />Miranda's friendship with downstairs neighbor Sal is suffering, and she's not sure why. And someone is leaving her weird little notes that have her freaking out. And this kid, Marcus, who punched Sal for no reason one time, suddenly is talking to her. <br />And then, there's the time travel stuff. Not much. I'm still wondering if it really works, in this book...<br />I'm thinking I missed something, that I'd benefit from a re-reading. Why do I think that? Because, I'm wondering about alternate timelines, which isn't good, is it? Shouldn't I be thinking about friendship, and sacrifice, and stuff?<br />Newbery winner 2010.</span>
  <a data-text-id="228928177361781084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86908305" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3191832-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463550510p2/3191832.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86908305?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/3191832-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

  <span id="freeText14815209316904060061" style="display:none">WOW. Holy cow. I did not see this coming. This was fantastic. This is going straight to my best of all time list. Very original, awesome setting. A very smart book. Great writing. LOVED it. Can't wait to read it again.<br /><br />Read it again. Just as good the second time.<br /><br />7/29/2014: My fourth read! Always amazing, but this time was really cool. My niece is at my house for a few days. She has to read this over the summer for school! We stayed up all night reading it right to the end. We both loved it. My voice is completely shot and my throat is raw from 2 solid hours of out-loud reading, but it was worth it. Of course I cried at THE LIST. I always do. I really tried not to. Gianna was cool about it. She knows her aunt is a leaky faucet! :) I'll always remember staying up late and snuggling with Gianna and reading this book, and how excited she was when she put it all together. I can't say it enough: this book is just so wonderful. </span>

<div id="review_2387898541" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2387898541" />
    <a title="Brierly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25485458-brierly"><img alt="Brierly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421634217p2/25485458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2387898541?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brierly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brierly" href="/user/show/25485458-brierly">Brierly</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/17826161-when-you-reach-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2387898541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10972714680372010956"><i>When You Reach Me</i> is a middle grades science fiction novel set in the late 20th century in the Upper West Side of New York City. The novel is a bit of a mystery, as well, as it focuses on the identity of the mysterious letter writer contacting sixth-grader Miranda. There are other elements woven in, additionally, including <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33574273.A_Wrinkle_in_Time__Time_Quintet___1_' title='A Wrinkle in Time (Time Quintet, #1) by Madeleine L'Engle' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Wrinkle in Time</a>, some time travel, and Jewish culture.<br/><br/>As a whole, this book had much to discuss (in a classroom) as far as plot, characters, and setting, despite being a qui</span>
  <span id="freeText10972714680372010956" style="display:none"><i>When You Reach Me</i> is a middle grades science fiction novel set in the late 20th century in the Upper West Side of New York City. The novel is a bit of a mystery, as well, as it focuses on the identity of the mysterious letter writer contacting sixth-grader Miranda. There are other elements woven in, additionally, including <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33574273.A_Wrinkle_in_Time__Time_Quintet___1_" title="A Wrinkle in Time (Time Quintet, #1) by Madeleine L'Engle" rel="nofollow noopener">A Wrinkle in Time</a>, some time travel, and Jewish culture.<br /><br />As a whole, this book had much to discuss (in a classroom) as far as plot, characters, and setting, despite being a quick read. Good for a middle school audience, but not exceptional otherwise. I listened to the audiobook edition.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10972714680372010956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2457448001" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2457448001" />
    <a title="Catie Currie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27455185-catie-currie"><img alt="Catie Currie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498971951p2/27455185.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2457448001?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie Currie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie Currie" href="/user/show/27455185-catie-currie">Catie Currie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27455185-catie-currie?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27455185-catie-currie?shelf=funny">funny</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2457448001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1310533811362316011">This was such a good book! I've learned to be wary of Newberry winners because, for some reason, they tend to be awful, but this one was so wonderful! It was well-written, touched on a lot of sticky issues in a really open, but tactful way, and the first person narration felt very authentic. The "twist" was fairly obvious to an adult, but I have no doubt that lots of kids' jaws dropped. I will definitely be recommending this book to all the middle schoolers I know.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82582982" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82582982" />
    <a title="Sarah BT" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2438338-sarah-bt"><img alt="Sarah BT" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299691396p2/2438338.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82582982?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah BT" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah BT" href="/user/show/2438338-sarah-bt">Sarah BT</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82582982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9790130173805498898"> I read this book many months ago, but I've held off on blogging about it because I didn't find myself gushing over it like everyone else and I wanted to think about why. I enjoyed it, and I think it's a good read, and I'm featuring it on Tween Tuesday because I think some tweens will enjoy it. It just didn't strike me as a book that could have a huge tween audience. If you have a tween reader who has enjoyed books by Kate DiCamillo, Sharon Creech, or Katherine Patterson, I would give them this </span>
  <span id="freeText9790130173805498898" style="display:none"> I read this book many months ago, but I've held off on blogging about it because I didn't find myself gushing over it like everyone else and I wanted to think about why. I enjoyed it, and I think it's a good read, and I'm featuring it on Tween Tuesday because I think some tweens will enjoy it. It just didn't strike me as a book that could have a huge tween audience. If you have a tween reader who has enjoyed books by Kate DiCamillo, Sharon Creech, or Katherine Patterson, I would give them this one. <br /><br />I was excited to read a book about time travel, especially one that featured a main character who was an avid reader and who was a fan of a book I loved as a tween. But unfortunately, I never felt like I connected to Miranda. She just never appealed to me. But, I'm also an adult, and I think readers who are in the same situation and trying to figure out friendships, may find solace in Miranda's struggles. <br /><br />I'm also a huge fan of time travel books, but I thought the time travel element never really worked. It felt very subtle to me, and since I was really looking forward to that aspect, it fell flat for me. I also wonder how much of the time period tween readers will understand-how many of them even know what the $20,000 Pyramid is? <br /><br />I did enjoy this one, I just wasn't blown away by it. It's a quick read and I think the author makes some great statements about friendships. I really enjoyed Miranda's friendship with Annemarie and I loved the relationship between Miranda's mom and her boyfriend Richard-her mom wasn't using him to get ahead or needed him financially, she could stand on her own, thank you very much.<br /><br />Really, I wouldn't be surprised if the Newbery buzz on this one comes true. It really struck me as a typical Newbery novel-one that adults, librarians and teachers love much more than the kids themselves. I'm not saying there won't be tweens who read this one and love it, I just don't think it will be adored as much by the tweens who read it. Maybe my expectations were too high after hearing it was amazing from so many people. <br /><br />Since every review I've seen of this one has come from an adult, I'd really love to hear a tween's reaction to this one!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9790130173805498898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nowwgWlcCk0I5PMmBTaMG+0P1tLiB7cEyiySE1R3cB6kqllT0gLDJa/PR0fyw4bEO1AxGiyKOWORUtSimTSChA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QvEVOv8nQ7qAKqIEUdzrnJl9pQ3kWc2aKCq2ERCFhXZ413zoRHmK0icBFmWmKeFDTyJCxSrUQ/1zVPCg3cZ37A==')})
  }

Snyder did when he joined it;• German atrocities toward captured crew and civilians;• behind-the-scenes stories of the Belgium civilians who risked all to save American flyers who were in the air one moment, spiraling down in flames the next;• creation and dedication of the monument to the Susan Ruth and its crew located in Macquenoise, Belgium in 1989.Shot Down was created from the vast number of letters and journals of Howard Snyder; diaries of men and women on the ground who rescued, sheltered and hid the crew; and interviews conducted by historians. Centered around the 306th Bomb Group in Thurleigh, England, it is informative, insightful and captivating.For most, 70 years is a long time ago. World War II fades in importance as each year goes by. Shot Down moves history out of the footnotes into reality, keeping the stories of real people alive as they experience being shot down. You are there, almost holding your breath as Lt.       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/6608018-when-you-reach-me">Quotes from When You Reach Me</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Well, it's simple to love someone," she said. "But it's hard to know when you need to say it out loud.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/209726-well-it-s-simple-to-love-someone-she-said-but-it-s">316 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Mom says each of us has a veil between ourselves and the rest of the world, like a bride wears on her wedding day, except this kind of veil is invisible. We walk around happily with these invisible veils hanging down over our faces. The world is kind of blurry, and we like it that way. But sometimes our veils are pushed away for a few moments, like there's a wind blowing it from our faces. And when the veil lifts, we can see the world as it really is, just for those few seconds before it settles down again. We see all the beauty, and cruelty, and sadness, and love. But mostly we are happy not to. Some people learn to lift the veil themselves. Then they don't have to depend on the wind anymore.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/224102-mom-says-each-of-us-has-a-veil-between-ourselves">270 likes</a>
            </nobr>
